Affirmation of Yad as an Eternal Attribute without Modality
The author affirms yad as an eternal attribute without how, referring to Allah's will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the attribute of yad (hand) is affirmed for Allah without modality and what it signifies.

Core Idea
Allah's 'hand' is an eternal attribute, not a limb — it points to His will.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi clarifies a crucial point about the divine attribute of yad (hand). He affirms it as an eternal attribute, like hearing and sight, but immediately strips it of any physical or modal interpretation. The passage draws a clear line between affirming what revelation says and avoiding anthropomorphism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the list of attributes and the repeated negation of modality.
Pay attention to the structure: first a list, then explanations, then a final interpretive statement.
2
Observe the negations
The author repeatedly says 'without modality' (بلا كيف) and 'without comparison' (بلا تشبيه). Identify all instances and note how they apply to each attribute.
This is the key to understanding the Ash'ari approach: affirm the attribute but negate any anthropomorphic implication.
3
Understand the final interpretation
The passage concludes: 'so by hand is expressed and what is meant is the will of Allah.' Ask yourself why the author offers this interpretation and how it connects to the broader theme of divine transcendence.
This interpretive move preserves the textual expression while avoiding any notion of a physical hand.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واليد من الصفات الأزلية بلا كيف ولا تشبيه، كالسمع والبصر، والعلم، والقدرة، والحياة، والإرادة، والكلام. فإن الله تعالى سميع بلا جارحة، بصير بلا عين عالم بلا آلة مريد بلا قلب متكلم بلا لسان وشفتين، وكذلك اليد من صفاته الأزلية بلا كيف وتشبيه وجارحة، فعبر باليد والمراد به إرادة الله تعالى.

Indeed Allah is Hearing without a limb, Seeing without an eye, Knowing without an instrument, Willing without a heart, Speaking without a tongue and lips. Likewise the hand is among His eternal attributes without modality, comparison, or limb. So by 'hand' is expressed and what is meant is the will of Allah.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a definition and affirmation of the attribute of yad (hand) of Allah. The author lists it among the eternal attributes (صفات أزلية) that are affirmed for Allah without modality (بلا كيف) and without comparison to creation (بلا تشبيه). He draws an analogy with other attributes: just as Allah's hearing is not through a physical ear, His seeing not through an eye, His knowledge not through a tool, His will not through a heart, His speech not through a tongue, so too His hand is not a limb or body part. The author then clarifies that when the term 'hand' appears in revelation, it signifies Allah's will (إرادة). This interpretation avoids anthropomorphism (تشبيه) while preserving the textual expression.

Refuting the Dual Interpretation of Divine Attributes
Refutation of Ibn Uthaymin's dual interpretation using Qur'anic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why insisting on a literal dual interpretation of God's attributes (like hand and eye) leads to inconsistency with Qur'anic usage and undermines tanzih (transcendence).

Core Idea
Qur'an uses 'yad' and 'ayn' in singular, dual, and plural—proving they are not literal limbs.

This lesson examines a key critique against literalist interpretations of divine attributes. Imam al-Nasafi demonstrates that the Qur'an itself uses the terms 'hand' and 'eye' in multiple grammatical forms, showing they cannot be taken as physical limbs. The argument serves to defend the principle of tanzih—God's transcendence over all creaturely qualities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the rhetorical question opening.
2
Identify the Qur'anic forms
List the verses cited for 'ayn' (singular) and 'yad' (singular, dual, plural). Observe the pattern.
The passage uses four verses for 'yad'.
3
Understand the logical problem
Consider why a literal dual interpretation conflicts with the use of singular and plural forms. The author argues this creates contradiction.
4
Reflect on tanzih
The passage concludes with Allah's transcendence. Think about how this refutation upholds tanzih.
Tanzih means removing any similarity to creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما قطع به الشيخ من تثنية العينين كيف يستقيم مع مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِتُصْنَعَ عَلَى عَيْنِي﴾ فقد وردت الآية بصيغة المفرد، فكيف يستقيم نص الآية مع فهم الشيخ ابن عثيمين؟ وهذا ينطبق على ما ورد في شأن اليد كذلك، فتارة يعبر القرءان عن اليد بصيغة المفرد كقوله: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يُبَايِعُونَكَ إِنَّمَا يُبَايِعُونَ اللَّهَ يَدُ اللَّهِ فَوقَ أَيْدِيهِم﴾ وتارة بصيغة التثنية كقوله: ﴿بَلْ يَدَاهُ مَبْسُوطَتَانِ يُنفِقُ كَيْفَ يَشَاءُ﴾ وتارةً بصيغة الجمع كقوله: ﴿ وَالسَّمَاءَ بَنَيْنَهَا بِأَيْيْدِ وَإِنَّا لَمُوسِعُونَ ﴾ وقوله: ﴿أَوَلَمْ يَرَوْا أَنَّا خَلَقْنَا لَهُم مِّمَّا عَمِلَتْ أَيْدِينَا أَنْعَمَّا فَهُمْ لَهَا مَلِكُونَ ﴾ فعلى ما يقول به ابن عثيمين ومن ينحو هذا المنحى سيقع التضارب في صفات الله تعالى، والله تعالى منزّه عن الصور والأشكال والحوادث والأعراض، تعالى الله عما يقول الظالمون علوا كبيرًا.
And what the shaykh [Ibn Uthaymin] has asserted of the duality of the two eyes, how can it be consistent with such as the saying of Allah Most High: 'And that you be formed under My eye' (20:39)? The verse came in the singular form, so how can the text of the verse be consistent with the understanding of Shaykh Ibn Uthaymin? And this applies to what is related concerning the hand as well. Sometimes the Qur'an expresses the hand in the singular form, like His saying: 'Indeed, those who pledge allegiance to you, they are only pledging allegiance to Allah. The hand of Allah is above their hands' (48:10); sometimes in the dual form, like His saying: 'Nay, both His hands are outstretched, He spends how He wills' (5:64); and sometimes in the plural form, like His saying: 'And the heaven We built with hands, and indeed We are the expanders' (51:47) and His saying: 'Do they not see that We have created for them from what Our hands have made, livestock, and they are their owners?' (36:71). So according to what Ibn Uthaymin and those who follow this path say, contradiction will occur in the attributes of Allah Most High. And Allah Most High is transcendent above forms, shapes, accidents, and events. Exalted is Allah far above what the wrongdoers say—a great exaltation.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the position held by Ibn Uthaymin (and those like him) who insist on interpreting 'yad' (hand) and 'ayn' (eye) as literally two hands and two eyes. The author argues that this interpretation contradicts the Qur'anic usage where these terms appear in singular, dual, and plural forms. He provides examples: for 'ayn' (eye) in the singular from Surah Ta-Ha (20:39); for 'yad' (hand), he cites verses using singular (48:10), dual (5:64), and plural (51:47, 36:71). If one insists on a literal dual meaning, then the singular and plural uses become problematic and lead to inconsistency in understanding Allah's attributes. The author concludes by affirming Allah's transcendence (تنزيه) above forms (صور), shapes (أشكال), and temporal or accidental attributes (حوادث وأعراض), declaring that such contradictory views are unjust.

Key Terms
تثنية (duality)
عين (eye)
يد (hand)
صيغة المفرد (singular form)
صيغة التثنية (dual form)
صيغة الجمع (plural form)
تنزيه (transcendence)
ابن عثيمين (Ibn Uthaymin)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dual forms for 'yad' and 'ayn' in the Qur'an prove that Allah literally has two hands and two eyes as physical organs.
Correction: The Qur'an uses these terms in singular, dual, and plural forms, showing they cannot be taken literally; they are expressions of divine power and care, not limbs.

D) Because it is not based on hadith

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's use of singular, dual, and plural forms for divine attributes like hand and eye refutes literal bipartite interpretations and upholds tanzih.

Refutation of the Mu'tazilite Interpretation of Yad as Power
Refutation of the Mu'tazilite interpretation of 'yad' as power using the dual form.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazilite interpretation of 'yad' as power is logically inconsistent with the Qur'anic use of the dual form.

Core Idea
If 'yad' means power, then 'two hands' would mean two powers, but Allah's power is one and indivisible.

The Mu'tazila claimed that the Qur'anic term 'yad' (hand) should be understood as power, strength, or grace. They pointed to verses like 'His two hands are outstretched' as evidence. In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi refutes this interpretation by focusing on another verse where Allah says He created with 'My two hands'—showing that the dual form cannot mean two powers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic original and the translation carefully. Notice how the author presents the Mu'tazilite claim first, then responds.
2
Identify the key proof
Find the verse cited by the author (38:75) and understand how the author uses the dual form to argue against the Mu'tazilite interpretation.
The verse uses 'بيدي' (with My two hands).
3
Analyze the logical inference
Follow the author's reasoning: if 'yad' is power, then 'two hands' implies two powers. But Allah's power is one, eternal, and not subject to division. Why is this a problem?
The author contrasts created attributes (accidents) with divine power.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider what this argument teaches about how we interpret anthropomorphic expressions in the Qur'an. The author upholds divine transcendence while rejecting a purely metaphorical reading that leads to inconsistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالت المعتزلة : المراد من اليد إنما القدرة والقوة والنعمة. وقال الله تعالى: يَدَاهُ مَبْسُوطَتَانِ ﴾ [المائدة: ٦٤] بمعني نعمتاه. فنقول : لا يجوز أن يقال بأن المراد من اليد القدرة والقوة، لأن الله تعالى قال: مَنَعَكَ أَن تَسْجُدَ لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَى [ص: ٧٥] ولو كان المراد من اليد إنما هو القوة والقدرة لكان ذلك قوتين وقدرتين وهذا لا يجوز لأن قوة الله تعالى وقدرته واحد لا يفنى ولا ينقطع، بخلاف قوة المخلوقين، لأن صفاتنا أعراض، والعرض لا يبقى زمانين، وقوة الله تعالى وقدرته ليست بعرض لا ينقطع ولا ينقص.
And the Mu'tazila said: What is meant by 'yad' is only power, strength, and grace. And Allah said: 'His two hands are outstretched' (5:64) meaning His two graces. We say: It is not permissible to say that what is meant by 'yad' is power and strength, because Allah said: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands?' (38:75). If what was meant by 'yad' were power and strength, then that would be two powers and two strengths, and that is not permissible because the power and strength of Allah are one, neither perishing nor ceasing, unlike the power of creatures because our attributes are accidents, and the accident does not remain for two moments. And the power and strength of Allah are not an accident that ceases or diminishes.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite interpretation that the word 'yad' (hand) in the Qur'an denotes power (قدرة), strength (قوة), or grace (نعمة). The author cites their proof from Surah Al-Ma'idah (5:64) where 'both His hands are outstretched' is interpreted as 'His two graces'. Then the author presents a counter-argument using Surah Sad (38:75): 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands?' (خلقت بيدي). If 'yad' meant power, then 'two hands' would imply two powers. But Allah's power is one, eternal, and indivisible; it does not perish or cease. In contrast, the attributes of creatures are accidents (أعراض) that do not persist for two moments. Since Allah's power is not an accident and does not diminish, the dual form cannot be taken literally as two powers. Therefore, the Mu'tazilite interpretation leads to an impossibility and is rejected.

قدرة (power)
قوة (strength)
نعمة (grace)
عرض (accident)
المعتزلة (Mu'tazila)
صفات (attributes)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qur'anic term 'yad' (hand) can be interpreted as power, strength, or grace without any theological inconsistency.
Correction: The author shows that interpreting 'yad' as power leads to a contradiction when applied to the dual form 'يَدَى' (two hands) in Surah Sad 38:75, because it would imply two distinct powers, whereas Allah's power is one and indivisible.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The dual form 'two hands' in the Qur'an precludes interpreting 'yad' as power, because Allah's power is one and indivisible.

The Four Meanings of Yad in the Qur'an
The author enumerates four meanings of yad in the Qur'an: sovereignty, grace, sin, and limb, the last negated from Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four distinct meanings of the word 'yad' as used in the Qur'an and why the literal limb meaning is negated from Allah.

Core Idea
The Qur'an uses 'yad' in four ways; only one is a limb, and it is negated from Allah.

The Arabic word 'yad' (hand) appears in the Qur'an in several senses. To understand the divine attribute of 'hand' correctly, we must distinguish these meanings. The author of this passage enumerates four distinct aspects of 'yad' as they occur in revelation and Arabic usage. By examining each with scriptural examples, we learn how to affirm Allah's attribute while safeguarding His transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the structure: the author first mentions 'qawlān' (the two sayings) and then lists four aspects.
2
Identify the four categories
Find the four meanings: sovereignty, favor, sin/act, and limb. Note the Quranic evidence provided for each.
The limb meaning is explicitly negated from Allah.
3
Understand the conclusion
The final sentence asserts that Allah's hand and His sovereignty are eternal attributes without modality, form, or limb. Reflect on why this distinction matters for Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك الكلام بأن الله تعالى متكلم بكلام واحدٍ وكلامه لا ينقطع، ثم اليد في القولين على أربعة أوجه منها الملك كقوله تعالى: ﴿تَبَارَكَ الَّذِي بِيَدِهِ الْمُلْكُ﴾ [الملك: 1] أي له الملك، ويقال: هذه القرية في يد فلان أي في ملكه وتصرفه. ومنها: المنة كقوله تعالى: ﴿يَدُ اللهِ فَوْقَ أَيْدِيهِمْ﴾ [الفتح: 10] أي منه الله فوق منتهم يعني التوحيد وقوله تعالى: ﴿مِمَّا عَمِلَتْ أَيْدِينَا أَنْعَامًا فَهُمْ لَهَا مَالِكُونَ﴾ [يس: 71] أي منة الله وأياديه. وفي الخبر: «اللهم لا تجعل لفاجر عندي يداً» أي منة، ومنها: المعصية كقوله تعالى: ﴿فَبِمَا كَسَبَتْ أَيْدِيكُمْ﴾ [الشورى: 30]. ومنها: الجارحة وهي اليمين والشمال والله منزّه عن الآخرين، وهذان [ أي يد الله وملكه ] بلا كيف وتشبيه وصورة وجارحة، وهي من صفات الأزلية.
And likewise the speech that Allah is speaking with one speech and His speech does not cease. Then the 'yad' according to the two sayings has four aspects: among them is sovereignty (al-mulk), like His saying: 'Blessed is He in Whose hand is the sovereignty' (67:1), meaning for Him is the sovereignty. And it is said: this village is in the hand of so-and-so, meaning in his possession and control. Among them is favor (al-minnah), like His saying: 'The hand of Allah is above their hands' (48:10), meaning the favor of Allah is above their favor, that is, monotheism; and His saying: 'From what Our hands have made, livestock, and they are their owners' (36:71), meaning the favor of Allah and His gifts. And in the tradition: 'O Allah, do not put for a wicked person a hand (i.e., favor) with me' meaning a favor. Among them is sin/act (al-ma'siya), like His saying: 'For what your hands have earned' (42:30). Among them is the limb (al-jāriḥa), which is the right and left, and Allah is transcendent above the two [i.e., limbs]. And these two [meaning the hand of Allah and His sovereignty] are without modality, comparison, form, or limb, and they are among the eternal attributes.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage classifies the different meanings of the word 'yad' as used in the Qur'an and Arabic language. The author presents four aspects: (1) Sovereignty (الملك), as in 'In Whose hand is the sovereignty' and the common expression 'in the hand of' meaning under one's control. (2) Favor/grace (المنة), as in 'The hand of Allah is above their hands' meaning His favor, and in the hadith asking not to put a 'hand' (favor) of a wicked person over the suppliant. (3) Sin or action (المعصية), as in 'what your hands have earned' meaning what you have done. (4) The literal limb (الجارحة), i.e., the right and left hand, which is negated from Allah. The author concludes that when the term 'yad' is used for Allah, it is an eternal attribute affirmed without modality, comparison, form, or limb. The mention of 'القولين' (the two sayings) may refer to the two positions (affirming the attribute vs. interpreting metaphorically), and the four aspects apply to both interpretations. The final sentence confirms that Allah's hand and His sovereignty are eternal attributes without modality or form.

Key Terms
يد (yad)
ملك (sovereignty)
منة (favor/grace)
معصية (sin/act)
جارحة (limb)
صفات أزلية (eternal attributes)
كيف (modality)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'yad' in the Qur'an always refers to a physical hand or limb.
Correction: The author shows that 'yad' has four distinct meanings: sovereignty, favor, sin/act, and limb. The limb meaning is only one of these and is explicitly negated from Allah. When referring to Allah, 'yad' is an eternal attribute without modality or form.

Checkpoint

A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The word 'yad' has four distinct meanings in the Qur'an, and Allah's 'yad' is an eternal attribute affirmed without modality, form, or limb.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Refuting the Mu'tazila Interpretation of 'Yad' as Power
Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazila interpretation of 'yad' as power/strength.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila interpretation of 'yad' as power/strength is invalid according to Nasafi, based on the Quranic verse and the nature of God's attributes.

Core Idea
God’s power is one and eternal, so 'yad' cannot mean multiple powers.

The Mu'tazila claimed that the divine attribute 'yad' (hand) in the Quran actually refers to power, strength, and grace. Nasafi refutes this by exposing a contradiction: if 'yad' meant power, then 'created with My two hands' would imply two powers, but God's power is singular and unchanging. This lesson examines his argument and the underlying theological principles.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila claim
Read the first sentence of the Arabic passage and its translation to understand what the Mu'tazila are saying.
Notice they base their interpretation on a Quranic verse about 'two hands outstretched'.
2
Examine Nasafi's counterargument
Identify the key Quranic verse Nasafi uses and his logical deduction: if 'yad' means power, then two hands means two powers, which is impossible for God.
The verse is from Surah Sad, verse 75.
3
Understand the nature of God's power
Notice Nasafi's distinction between God's attributes (eternal, not accidents) and created attributes (accidents that perish). This strengthens his refutation.
Accidents (a'rad) are temporary; God's power is not an accident.
4
Reflect on the theological principle
Why does the oneness of God require a single power? This is a core kalam principle.
The unity of God (tawhid) implies unity in attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَتِ الْمُعْتَزِلَةُ: الْمُرَادُ مِنَ الْيَدِ إِنَّمَا الْقُدْرَةُ وَالْقُوَّةُ وَالنِّعْمَةُ. وَقَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {يَدَاهُ مَبْسُوطَتَانِ} بِمَعْنَى نِعْمَتَاهُ. فَنَقُولُ: لَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يُقَالَ بِأَنَّ الْمُرَادَ مِنَ الْيَدِ الْقُدْرَةُ وَالْقُوَّةُ، لِأَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى قَالَ: {مَنَعَكَ أَنْ تَسْجُدَ لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ} وَلَوْ كَانَ الْمُرَادُ مِنَ الْيَدِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ الْقُوَّةُ وَالْقُدْرَةُ لَكَانَ ذَلِكَ قُوَّتَيْنِ وَقُدْرَتَيْنِ وَهَذَا لَا يَجُوزُ لِأَنَّ قُوَّةَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَقُدْرَتَهُ وَاحِدٌ لَا يَفْنَى وَلَا يَنْقَطِعُ، بِخِلَافِ قُوَّةِ الْمَخْلُوقِينَ، لِأَنَّ صِفَاتِنَا أَعْرَاضٌ، وَالْعَرَضُ لَا يَبْقَى زَمَانَيْنِ، وَقُوَّةُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَقُدْرَتُهُ لَيْسَتْ بِعَرَضٍ لَا يَنْقَطِعُ وَلَا يَنْقُصُ.
And the Mu'tazila said: The intended meaning of 'hand' is only power, strength, and grace. And Allah the Exalted said: 'His two hands are outstretched' in the sense of His two graces. So we say: It is not permissible to say that the intended meaning of 'hand' is power and strength, because Allah the Exalted said: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands?' And if the intended meaning of 'hand' were only strength and power, that would be two strengths and two powers, and this is not permissible because the strength of Allah the Exalted and His power are one, neither perishing nor ceasing, unlike the strength of creatures, because our attributes are accidents, and the accident does not remain for two moments, and the strength of Allah the Exalted and His power are not an accident, neither ceasing nor decreasing.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila interpretation of the divine attribute 'yad' (hand). The author first states their position: that 'yad' in the Quran means power (qudra), strength (quwwa), and grace (ni'ma). They cite the verse 'His two hands are outstretched' as meaning His two graces. Then Nasafi responds by invalidating this interpretation. He argues that if 'yad' meant power/strength, then the verse 'created with My two hands' would imply two powers or two strengths. But God's power is single and unitary, not multiple. Furthermore, created attributes are accidents (a'rad) which do not persist for two moments, whereas God's power is eternal and not an accident. Thus the Mu'tazila view leads to a contradiction regarding God's unity and the nature of His attributes.

القدرة
القوة
النعمة
العرض

Correction: Nasafi shows this leads to multiple powers, contradicting God's oneness and the eternal nature of His attributes.

The Four Meanings of 'Yad' in Scripture
Nasafi enumerates four meanings of 'yad' and applies them to God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four distinct meanings of the Arabic word 'yad' as used in the Quran and how they apply to Allah without anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
The word 'yad' in the Quran has multiple meanings; when attributed to Allah, it is an eternal attribute without physicality.

Nasafi clarifies a common confusion: the Arabic word 'yad' does not always mean a physical hand. In the Quran, it appears in several senses. This lesson unpacks the four meanings he identifies, showing how the same word can refer to power, blessings, wrongdoing, or a limb, and how we affirm only the appropriate meanings for Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall classification.
Notice the four 'minha' markers that introduce each meaning.
2
Identify the four meanings
List each meaning with its scriptural evidence: kingdom, grace, sin, and limb. Notice how each is supported by a Quranic verse or hadith.
3
Understand which apply to Allah
Nasafi explicitly negates the limb meaning for Allah and affirms kingdom and grace as eternal attributes without modality.
This guards against anthropomorphism.
4
Reflect on the principle of bila kayf
The passage concludes with 'without how, comparison, form, or limb'. Consider why this is important for tawhid.
These attributes are affirmed without questioning the 'how'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الْيَدُ فِي الْقَوْلَيْنِ عَلَى أَرْبَعَةِ أَوْجُهٍ: مِنْهَا الْمُلْكُ كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: {تَبَارَكَ الَّذِي بِيَدِهِ الْمُلْكُ} أَيْ لَهُ الْمُلْكُ، وَيُقَالُ: هَذِهِ الْقَرْيَةُ فِي يَدِ فُلَانٍ أَيْ فِي مِلْكِهِ وَتَصَرُّفِهِ. وَمِنْهَا: الْمِنَّةُ كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: {يَدُ اللَّهِ فَوْقَ أَيْدِيهِمْ} أَيْ مِنَّةُ اللَّهِ فَوْقَ مِنَّتِهِمْ يَعْنِي التَّوْحِيدَ، وَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: {مِمَّا عَمِلَتْ أَيْدِينَا أَنْعَامًا فَهُمْ لَهَا مَالِكُونَ} أَيْ مِنَّةُ اللَّهِ وَأَيَادِيهِ. وَفِي الْخَبَرِ: «اللَّهُمَّ لَا تَجْعَلْ لِفَاجِرٍ عِنْدِي يَدًا» أَيْ مِنَّةً. وَمِنْهَا: الْمَعْصِيَةُ كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: {فَبِمَا كَسَبَتْ أَيْدِيكُمْ}. وَمِنْهَا: الْجَارِحَةُ وَهِيَ الْيَمِينُ وَالشِّمَالُ، وَاللَّهُ مُنَزَّهٌ عَنِ الْآخَرَيْنِ، وَهَذَانِ [أَيْ يَدُ اللَّهِ وَمِلْكُهُ] بِلَا كَيْفٍ وَتَشْبِيهٍ وَصُورَةٍ وَجَارِحَةٍ، وَهِيَ مِنْ صِفَاتِ الْأَزَلِيَّةِ.
Then 'hand' in the two positions has four aspects: among them is kingdom, as His saying the Exalted: 'Blessed is He in whose hand is the kingdom' meaning to Him belongs the kingdom, and it is said: this village is in the hand of so-and-so, meaning in his possession and control. And among them is grace, as His saying the Exalted: 'The hand of Allah is above their hands' meaning the grace of Allah is above their grace, meaning tawhid, and His saying the Exalted: 'Of what Our hands have wrought cattle, so they are their owners' meaning the grace of Allah and His favors. And in the report: 'O Allah, do not place a hand of a sinful person upon me' meaning a favor. And among them is sin, as His saying the Exalted: 'Because of what your hands have earned.' And among them is the limb, which is the right and left, and Allah is exalted above the other two, and these two [i.e., the hand of Allah and His kingdom] are without how, comparison, form, or limb, and they are among the eternal attributes.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the four meanings of the word 'yad' (hand) as used in the Quran and Arabic language. The author lists them: (1) Kingdom (mulk), exemplified by the verse 'In His hand is the kingdom' and the idiomatic expression 'this village is in the hand of so-and-so'; (2) Grace (minna), as in 'the hand of Allah is above their hands' meaning His favor, and the hadith asking not to let a sinner have a 'hand' (favor) over the speaker; (3) Sin (ma'siya), as in 'because of what your hands have earned'; (4) Limb (jariba), i.e., the physical hand. The author then clarifies that when these meanings are applied to Allah, the last one (limb) is negated, and the first two (kingdom and grace) are affirmed as eternal attributes without modality (bila kayf), comparison (tashbih), form (sura), or limb (jariba). This guards against anthropomorphism while affirming the reality of God's attributes.

Key Terms
اليد
الملك
المنة
المعصية
الجارحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'yad' always means a physical hand.
Correction: Nasafi shows that 'yad' has multiple meanings in the Quran and Arabic, and when applied to God it is a transcendental attribute, not a physical limb.

Checkpoint
How many meanings of 'yad' does Nasafi list?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The word 'yad' has four meanings in the Quran, and when attributed to Allah, it refers to His kingdom and grace as eternal attributes without physicality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself picturing Allah with a hand like ours? How does this passage challenge that image, and what does it mean for your relationship with a God who is beyond physical form?
?
When you recite 'يد الله فوق أيديهم', do you feel that Allah's grace overshadows your own efforts? How would your daily reliance on Him change if you truly internalized that His 'hand' is not a hand but His eternal favor?
?
Nasafi insists that Allah's attributes are 'without how' (بلا كيف). Are you comfortable worshipping a God whose attributes you cannot fully imagine? What does this teach you about humility and faith?

Allah's Manifestation to the Believers on Judgment Day
Nasafi explains a hadith about Allah's self-disclosure on the Day of Resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith about Allah's manifestation on Judgment Day and how believers recognize Him through His attributes.

Core Idea
Allah’s attributes of mercy are familiar; His attributes of power may surprise.

In this brief passage, Imam Nasafi unpacks a profound hadith about the Day of Resurrection: Allah manifests Himself in attributes the believers did not associate with Him in this world, leading to a moment of confusion before they recognize Him through His familiar mercy. This lesson explores how the beatific vision is understood in Sunni theology as a manifestation of attributes, not a physical form.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the narrative of Allah's manifestation in two stages.
Pay attention to the sequence: first power/justice, then mercy.
2
Identify the two stages
Note the first stage: Allah shows attributes of politics, justice, splitting of the moon, falling stars. The second stage: He shows forgiveness and pardon.
These represent different aspects of His divine attributes.
3
Understand the theological point
The believers knew Allah only by forgiveness and generosity in this world, so when He manifests in power, they do not immediately recognize Him.
This underscores that our knowledge of Allah is limited in this life.
4
Address the misconception
This passage does not imply Allah has a physical form; rather, it describes the manifestation of His attributes.
Sunni theology affirms the beatific vision without physicality.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this shapes our understanding of Allah's self-disclosure on Judgment Day.
The recognition is through attributes, not a literal form.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يتجلّي على صورة يعرفونه أي على صفة لا يعرفونه في الدنيا، لأنهم عرفوه في الدنيا بالتجاوز والكرم، فإذا أظهر السياسة والعدل، وانشقاق القمر، وسقوط النجوم، فيقول العباد يا ربنا ما عرفناك في الدنيا بهذه الصفة، ثم يظهر التجاوز والعفو فيقولون: عرفناك بهذه الصفة.
Then He manifests in a form they recognize, i.e. in a description they do not know in this world, because they knew Him in this world by forgiveness and generosity. So when He shows politics and justice, and the splitting of the moon, and the falling of stars, the servants say: 'O our Lord, we did not know You in this world with this description.' Then He shows forgiveness and pardon, and they say: 'We know You with this description.'
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a brief explanation of a hadith about the beatific vision. The author describes two stages: first, Allah manifests in attributes of power and justice that the believers did not associate with Him in the world (since they knew Him only by mercy), causing temporary confusion. Then He manifests in His familiar attributes of forgiveness and pardon, and they recognize Him. The passage stresses that Allah is not physically seen; rather, His attributes are manifested.

Key Terms
التجلي
الصورة
الرؤية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah has a physical form or that the manifestation is a literal visible shape.
Correction: The manifestation is of divine attributes, not a physical form. This is consistent with Sunni theology that affirms the beatific vision without corporeality.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do the servants initially say they did not know Allah in the world with that description?
A) Because they had never heard of His attributes.
B) Because they only knew Him by forgiveness and generosity, not by justice and power.
C) Because they were not believers.
D) Because the hadith is not authentic.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of manifestation teaches that on Judgment Day, believers will recognize Allah through His familiar attributes of mercy, after momentarily being confronted by His attributes of power and justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever only known Allah by His mercy, neglecting His justice? How would you feel if He showed you His politics and justice before mercy on Judgment Day? Stop now and ask yourself: Are you relying on His mercy without taking His justice seriously?
?
When you read that the believers were confused by Allah's attributes of power, does it stir any fear in you about how you will respond when you see Him? What is your heart's true familiarity with Allah—only His forgiveness, or also His majesty?
?
The believers recognized Allah by His forgiveness. Is forgiveness the attribute that defines your relationship with Allah? Or have you taken His mercy for granted? Write one concrete change you will make today to honor both His justice and mercy.

Scholarly Critique of the Hadith of Manifestation
Al-Kawthari, Ibn Hazm, and Ibn al-ʿArabī interpret the hadith to avoid anthropomorphism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni scholars reconcile problematic hadith narrations through critical hadith methodology and figurative interpretation.

Core Idea
The hadith of Manifestation must be understood through transmission-by-meaning and figurative interpretation.

In this lesson, we explore the scholarly critique of the Hadith of Manifestation, a narration that appears to describe Allah in anthropomorphic terms. Trusted scholars like al-Kawthari, Ibn Hazm, and Ibn al-ʿArabī employ rigorous hadith criticism and theological reasoning to demonstrate that the literal wording cannot be taken at face value. Their analysis reveals the mature methodology of Sunni scholars in handling ambiguous texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Recognize the tension between the hadith's literal wording and established Quranic and theological principles.
The hadith mentions Allah appearing in a 'form', which seems anthropomorphic.
2
Understand al-Kawthari's argument
He points to transmission-by-meaning and the believers' lack of knowledge of Allah in a form to argue the wording is not literal.
Also notes the contradiction with the Quranic statement that hypocrites are veiled.
3
Explore Ibn Hazm's interpretation
He reinterprets 'form' as the 'form of the state' (terror/condition), not a physical form.
Uses the hadith's own phrase 'other than the one you knew' as evidence.
4
Note Ibn al-ʿArabī's consensus claim
He denies that any vision occurs at that moment, placing it only in Paradise, and critiques Ibn Rushd's contrary opinion.
This shows the importance of scholarly consensus in theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر الإمام البيهقي هذا الحديث في كتاب الأسماء والصفات وحاول أن يأوله تأويلاً يتناسب مع ما ثبت من الصفات التي تنبغي الله تعالى والتي تمتنع عليه سبحانه وتعالى، وقد أطال البحث في هذه المسألة في كتابه المشار إليه من ص ٢٧٨-٢٨٣.
وقد علق الإمام الكوثري رحمه الله تعالى على هذا الحديث تعليقا أحببت أن أنقله بكامله لنفاسته ودقته قال رحمه الله معلقا على الحديث ما صورته:
اضطربت الروايات في ذكر الصورة والإتيان كما يظهر من استعراض طرق هذا الحديث ومتونه في الصحيحين» و «جامع الترمذي» و «توحيد ابن خزيمة و سنن الدارمي وغيرها، ولم يسبق أن عرفوه على صورة، فعلم أنه قد فعلت الرواية بالمعنى في الحديث ما فعلت، على أن المنافقين محجبون عن ربهم يوم القيام، فيكون هذا الحديث مخالفًا لنص القرءان إلا عند من يأوله تأويلاً بعيدًا، فالقول الفصل هنا هو الإعراض عن ألفاظ انفرد بها هذا الراوي أو ذاك باختلافهم فيها، والأخذ بالقدر المشترك من المعنى الذي اتفقوا عليه فلعلك لا تجد في ذلك ما يوقعك في ريبة أو شبهة.
قال ابن حزم قد أخبر عليه السلام أن الله يبدو للمؤمن يوم القيامة في غير الصورة التي عرفوها، وهذا ظاهر بين، وهو أنهم يرون صورة الحال من الهول والمخافة غير التي يظنون في الدنيا وبرهان صحة هذا القول قوله الله في الحديث المذكور غير التي عرفتموه بها وبالضرورة نعلم أننا لم نعلم الله عز وجل في الدنيا صورة أصلاً، فصح ما ذكرنا يقيناً. انتهى. ويقول ابن العربي في عارضة الأحوذي إن الناس في هذه الحال لا يرونه سبحانه في قول العلماء، وإنما محل الرؤية الجنة .... بإجماع العلماء، وإنما هذه المراجعات بين بين الخلق وبين الواسطة انتهى. وهو أجد بالتعويل في نقل الإجماع من أمثال ابن رشد الحفيد الفيلسوف الظنين الذي يقول هنا ما يعاكس الحق انتقاما من المتكلمين انتهى.
Imam al-Bayhaqi mentioned this hadith in his book 'al-Asma' wa al-Sifat' and attempted to interpret it in a manner consistent with the established attributes befitting Allah and which are impossible for Him, and he lengthened the discussion on this issue in his aforementioned book from p. 278-283.
Imam al-Kawthari, may Allah have mercy on him, commented on this hadith with a commentary I wished to quote in full for its value and precision. He said, commenting on the hadith, its form:
The narrations vary regarding the mention of the 'form' and 'coming' as appears from reviewing the chains and texts of this hadith in the two Sahihs, Jami' al-Tirmidhi, Tawhid Ibn Khuzayma, Sunan al-Darimi and others. And they had never known Him before in a form, so it is known that transmission by meaning has done its work in the hadith. Moreover, the hypocrites are veiled from their Lord on the Day of Resurrection, so this hadith contradicts the text of the Quran except for one who interprets it with a far-fetched interpretation. So the decisive word here is to disregard expressions unique to this or that narrator due to their disagreement in them, and to take the common element of meaning upon which they agreed. Perhaps you will not find in that anything that puts you into doubt or suspicion.
Ibn Hazm said: The Prophet, peace be upon him, informed that Allah appears to the believer on the Day of Resurrection in other than the form they knew. This is clear and evident, meaning that they see a 'form of the state' of terror and fear other than what they supposed in the world. The proof of the correctness of this statement is the saying of Allah in the aforementioned hadith: 'Other than the one you knew Him by.' And necessarily we know that we never knew Allah, Mighty and Majestic, in the world as a form at all. So what we mentioned is established with certainty. End. And Ibn al-'Arabi says in 'Aridat al-Ahwadhi: People in this state do not see Him, exalted, according to the statement of the scholars; rather, the place of vision is Paradise... by consensus of the scholars. And these dialogues are between the creation and the intermediary. End. And he is more deserving to be relied upon in transmitting consensus than the likes of Ibn Rushd the grandson, the philosopher, the suspect, who says here the opposite of the truth out of vengeance against the theologians. End.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is an extended editorial commentary on the hadith from Lesson 1. It begins by noting al-Bayhaqi's attempt at interpretation. Then al-Kawthari's comment is quoted: he points out discrepancies in the narrations and argues that since the believers never knew Allah in a form in the world, the hadith must have been transmitted by meaning and thus its literal wording is unreliable. He also notes a conflict with the Quranic verse that hypocrites are veiled. Ibn Hazm is then quoted: he interprets the 'form' (surah) as a 'form of the state' (surah al-hal), i.e., the terrifying situation, not a physical form. Finally, Ibn al-'Arabi denies that any vision occurs at that moment, placing it only in Paradise, and he dismisses Ibn Rushd's contrary opinion as biased.

Key Terms
التأويل
الرواية بالمعنى
الصورة
المنافقون
الرؤية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the literal wording of the hadith is authoritative and must be taken at face value.
Correction: Scholars show that the hadith has been transmitted by meaning, its wording is not reliable, and it must be interpreted figuratively in line with Quran and theology.

Checkpoint
According to al-Kawthari, why is the hadith considered to have been transmitted by meaning?
A) Because the narrators were unreliable.
B) Because the believers had never known Allah in a form in the world.
C) Because the Quran does not mention it.
D) Because Imam al-Bayhaqi said so.

Key Takeaway
Sunni scholars resolve ambiguous hadith through critical analysis and figurative interpretation, preserving the transcendence of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt disturbed by a hadith that seems to describe Allah in human terms? After this lesson, will you trust the scholars' interpretations and the principle that Allah is beyond any resemblance?
?
Al-Kawthari warns that unique narrations can cause doubt if taken literally. Is there a specific hadith or belief about Allah's attributes that has unsettled you? Are you willing to set aside your initial impression and seek the understanding of the learned?
?
Ibn al-ʿArabī relies on consensus (ijma') to deny vision before Paradise. Do you have the patience to seek out and trust scholarly consensus when faced with difficult texts, or do you tend to rely on your own immediate understanding?

The Meaning of Istiwa': Domination, Not Settlement
Nasafi refutes the Karramiyyah claim of physical settlement on the Throne using linguistic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Karramiyyah interpretation of istiwa' is rejected and how linguistic evidence supports the interpretation of domination.

Core Idea
Istiwa' means domination, not physical settlement.

The Karramiyyah sect wrongly claimed that Allah physically settled on the Throne. Nasafi refutes this by citing exegetes who interpret istiwa' as istila' (domination), supported by a Persian translation and a line of poetry.

Guided Path
1
Read the Karramiyyah claim
Read the first sentence of the passage to understand the claim that Allah settled on the Throne and their proof from the Quran.
Notice that they interpret istiwa' literally.
2
Identify the refutation
Read the next part where Nasafi responds by citing exegetes who say istiwa' means domination (istila'), and note the Persian translation.
The Persian phrase means 'The King is dominant over His Throne'.
3
Examine the poetic evidence
Read the line of poetry and understand how it demonstrates that istiwa' can mean domination in Arabic usage.
The poet says 'Bishr has istawa over Iraq' meaning he dominated it without war.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان معنى الاستواء على العرش ]
قالت الكرَّامية : إن الله تعالى استقرَّ على العرش حتى امتلأ منه حجتهم قوله تعالى: ﴿الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ﴾ [طه: ٥].
قلنا لهم: قال بعض أهل التفسير : يعني استولى قيل : بالفارسية: بر عرش پادشاه است (١) وهي جملة فارسية معناها : الملك مستول على عرشه.
يدل عليه قول القائل:
قد استوى بشر على العِرَاقِ من غير سيف ودم مِهْرَاقِ
يعني: استولى.
قلت: وقد صدق الشيخ رحمه الله في قوله: «فعلِمَ أنه قد فعلت الرواية بالمعنى في الحديث ما فعلت» فمن المعلوم والمقرر أن جُلَّ السنة نقل بالمعنى، ومن هذا الباب حديث الجارية المشهور، فقد ورد في أحد طرقه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سألها «أين الله ؟ فأشارت إلى السماء؟» فهذا مما فعلت فيه الرواية بالمعنى ما فعلت أيضًا، لأن الرواية الأخرى لم يرد بها هذا السؤال الذي لم يرد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في أي حديث آخر، حيث كان لا يقبل إسلام من يُسلم دون مثل هذه الأسئلة التي لا تتفق مع ما يليق بالله عزّ وجل، فالله تعالى لا أين له حتى يُسأل عنه بالأين ، فهو خالق المكان والزمان وهو على ما عليه كان لم يتغير ولم يتبدل سبحانه وتعالى عما يصفون، وقد غابت هذه القاعدة عن أذهان كثيرن ممن تورّطوا في التشبيه. والله أعلى وأعلم.
Chapter on explaining the meaning of istiwa' over the Throne.
The Karramiyyah said: Allah settled on the Throne until He filled it; their proof is His saying: 'The Most Merciful istawa over the Throne' [Taha:5].
We said to them: Some of the exegetes said: It means He dominated. It is said in Persian: 'Bar 'arsh padshah ast' (١) and it is a Persian sentence meaning: The King is dominant over His Throne.
This is supported by the saying of the poet:
'Bishr has istawa over Iraq without sword and bloodshed'
meaning: He dominated.
I say: The Shaykh, may Allah have mercy on him, was correct in his saying: 'So it is known that transmission by meaning has done its work in the hadith.' It is well established that most of the Sunnah was transmitted by meaning. Among this is the famous hadith of the slave girl, for in one of its chains the Prophet, peace be upon him, asked her: 'Where is Allah?' and she pointed to the sky. This too is an instance where transmission by meaning did its work, because the other narration does not contain this question, which has not been reported from the Prophet, peace be upon him, in any other hadith. He would not accept someone's Islam without such questions that are inconsistent with what befits Allah, Mighty and Majestic. Allah does not have a 'where' such that He should be asked about it. He is the Creator of place and time, and He is as He ever was, unchanged and unaltered, exalted above what they describe. Many of those who fell into anthropomorphism have overlooked this principle. And Allah is Most High and Most Knowing.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Karramiyyah sect's literal interpretation of istiwa'. The author first states their claim that Allah physically settled on the Throne, citing the Quranic verse. The refutation begins by citing exegetes who interpret istiwa' as istila' (domination), supported by a Persian translation and a poetic line. The editor (likely the same as in Lesson 2) then reinforces the point by linking this to the principle of transmission by meaning, using the hadith of the slave girl as an example. The question 'Where is Allah?' in some narrations is argued to be a transmission by meaning, not the Prophet's actual words, because attributing a location to Allah is impermissible. The author concludes that many who fell into anthropomorphism neglected this principle.

Key Terms
الاستواء
الاستيلاء
العرش
الكرَّامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Istiwa' means physical sitting or settlement.
Correction: Istiwa' in this context means domination (istila'), as supported by exegesis and poetry.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the Karramiyyah claim about istiwa'?
A) By citing a hadith that denies it.
B) By offering linguistic and poetic evidence that istiwa' means domination.
C) By saying the verse is abrogated.
D) By claiming the Quran is unclear.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic istiwa' is interpreted by scholars as Allah's absolute dominion over the Throne, not physical settlement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The poet used the same word (istawa) for a human ruler. Do you ever describe Allah using language that could lower His majesty? What will you do to ensure your speech about Allah is free from anthropomorphism?
?
If someone insisted that the Quranic 'istiwa' implies Allah sitting on a throne, would you be equipped to respond with linguistic evidence? What step will you take to deepen your understanding of the divine attributes so you can defend tawhid?

Transmission by Meaning and the Hadith of the Slave Girl
Nasafi uses the hadith of the slave girl to illustrate how transmission by meaning can introduce problematic wording.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle of transmission by meaning and how it applies to the hadith about the slave girl, preserving Allah's transcendence beyond place.

Core Idea
Hadith transmitted by meaning may include wording that misrepresents Allah's attributes.

The editor expands on the principle that much of the Sunnah was transmitted by meaning. He uses the famous hadith of the slave girl to show that the question 'Where is Allah?' is a result of transmission by meaning, not the Prophet's actual words, because Allah is beyond location.

Guided Path
1
Read the editor's statement
Read the part starting with 'قلت: وقد صدق الشيخ رحمه الله' and note the principle of transmission by meaning.
The editor affirms that most of the Sunnah was transmitted by meaning.
2
Analyze the slave girl hadith example
Read how the hadith of the slave girl is presented as an instance of transmission by meaning, focusing on the question 'Where is Allah?'.
This question is not found in other narrations.
3
Understand the theological conclusion
Reflect on why asking 'Where is Allah?' is inappropriate and how this maintains Allah's transcendence.
Allah is the Creator of place and time, so He is not confined to any location.

فصل في بيان معنى الاستواء على العرش ]
قالت الكرَّامية : إن الله تعالى استقرَّ على العرش حتى امتلأ منه حجتهم قوله تعالى: ﴿الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ﴾ [طه: ٥].
قلنا لهم: قال بعض أهل التفسير : يعني استولى قيل : بالفارسية: بر عرش پادشاه است (١) وهي جملة فارسية معناها : الملك مستول على عرشه.

قد استوى بشر على العِرَاقِ من غير سيف ودم مِهْرَاقِ
يعني: استولى.
قلت: وقد صدق الشيخ رحمه الله في قوله: «فعلِمَ أنه قد فعلت الرواية بالمعنى في الحديث ما فعلت» فمن المعلوم والمقرر أن جُلَّ السنة نقل بالمعنى، ومن هذا الباب حديث الجارية المشهور، فقد ورد في أحد طرقه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سألها «أين الله ؟ فأشارت إلى السماء؟» فهذا مما فعلت فيه الرواية بالمعنى ما فعلت أيضًا، لأن الرواية الأخرى لم يرد بها هذا السؤال الذي لم يرد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في أي حديث آخر، حيث كان لا يقبل إسلام من يُسلم دون مثل هذه الأسئلة التي لا تتفق مع ما يليق بالله عزّ وجل، فالله تعالى لا أين له حتى يُسأل عنه بالأين ، فهو خالق المكان والزمان وهو على ما عليه كان لم يتغير ولم يتبدل سبحانه وتعالى عما يصفون، وقد غابت هذه القاعدة عن أذهان كثيرن ممن تورّطوا في التشبيه. والله أعلى وأعلم.
Chapter on explaining the meaning of istiwa' over the Throne.
The Karramiyyah said: Allah settled on the Throne until He filled it; their proof is His saying: 'The Most Merciful istawa over the Throne' [Taha:5].
We said to them: Some of the exegetes said: It means He dominated. It is said in Persian: 'Bar 'arsh padshah ast' (١) and it is a Persian sentence meaning: The King is dominant over His Throne.
This is supported by the saying of the poet:
'Bishr has istawa over Iraq without sword and bloodshed'
meaning: He dominated.
I say: The Shaykh, may Allah have mercy on him, was correct in his saying: 'So it is known that transmission by meaning has done its work in the hadith.' It is well established that most of the Sunnah was transmitted by meaning. Among this is the famous hadith of the slave girl, for in one of its chains the Prophet, peace be upon him, asked her: 'Where is Allah?' and she pointed to the sky. This too is an instance where transmission by meaning did its work, because the other narration does not contain this question, which has not been reported from the Prophet, peace be upon him, in any other hadith. He would not accept someone's Islam without such questions that are inconsistent with what befits Allah, Mighty and Majestic. Allah does not have a 'where' such that He should be asked about it. He is the Creator of place and time, and He is as He ever was, unchanged and unaltered, exalted above what they describe. Many of those who fell into anthropomorphism have overlooked this principle. And Allah is Most High and Most Knowing.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Karramiyyah sect's literal interpretation of istiwa'. The author first states their claim that Allah physically settled on the Throne, citing the Quranic verse. The refutation begins by citing exegetes who interpret istiwa' as istila' (domination), supported by a Persian translation and a poetic line. The editor (likely the same as in Lesson 2) then reinforces the point by linking this to the principle of transmission by meaning, using the hadith of the slave girl as an example. The question 'Where is Allah?' in some narrations is argued to be a transmission by meaning, not the Prophet's actual words, because attributing a location to Allah is impermissible. The author concludes that many who fell into anthropomorphism neglected this principle.

Key Terms
الأين
الرواية بالمعنى
الجارية
التشبيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith of the slave girl contains the Prophet's exact words, so Allah must have a location.
Correction: The question 'Where is Allah?' is likely a transmission by meaning; the original hadith probably did not contain such a question, as affirming bodily location contradicts Allah's transcendence.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about the hadith of the slave girl?
A) It proves that Allah is in the sky.
B) The question 'Where is Allah?' is part of the original hadith.
C) The wording is likely a result of transmission by meaning, not the Prophet's exact words.
D) The hadith is weak and should be rejected.

Key Takeaway
Transmission by meaning can introduce wording that conflicts with Allah's transcendence, so we rely on established principles of tawhid to interpret such narrations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a hadith that seems to describe Allah with human-like qualities, do you immediately accept it literally or do you investigate its authenticity and consider the principle of tanzih? What steps can you take to guard yourself from falling into anthropomorphism?
?
The editor warns that many fell into anthropomorphism by overlooking the principle of transmission by meaning. Have you ever uncritically accepted a religious text just because it is attributed to the Prophet? How can you develop a habit of verifying narrations against the clear principles of tawhid?
?
If a friend argues that the hadith of the slave girl proves Allah is in the sky, will you be able to explain the role of transmission by meaning and the transcendence of Allah? Write down exactly what you would say to them using specific points from this lesson.

Imam Malik's Statement on Istiwa: Affirming the Attribute Without Asking How
Imam Malik's authoritative statement on istiwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Malik's normative approach to the divine attribute of istiwa, and why questioning its modality is considered an innovation.

Core Idea
We affirm the meaning, but we do not ask how.

Imam Malik's famous statement sets a clear boundary for Sunni theology: the attribute of istiwa is affirmed, its modality is beyond human comprehension, and probing into the 'how' is a sign of misguidance. This passage is a cornerstone of the Sunni approach to divine attributes, emphasizing tafwid (consigning modality to Allah) while upholding the literal meaning of the Quranic text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully. Notice the four-part structure: istiwa is not unknown, modality is not comprehensible, belief is obligatory, asking is innovation.
The harsh response to the questioner is significant.
2
Identify the key components
Break down Imam Malik's statement into its four components: what we know, what we don't know, what we must do, and what we must avoid. Also note the identification of the questioner as Jahm ibn Safwan.
3
Understand the theological significance
Reflect on why this statement is so important in Sunni creed. It establishes a middle path between denial (ta'til) and anthropomorphism (tashbih). The questioner is the founder of the Jahmiyya sect.
This statement is often cited in discussions of divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن مالك بن أنس رضي الله عنه إمام أهل المدينة أنه قال: «الاستواء غير مجهول، والكيف غير معقول ، والإيمان به واجب، والسؤال عنه بدعة، وقال للسائل : ما أراك إلا ضالاً. وأمره بالصفع (۱) فإذا هو جهم بن صفوان عليه اللعنة».
And from Malik ibn Anas (may Allah be pleased with him), the imam of the people of Medina, that he said: 'The istiwa is not unknown, the modality is not comprehensible, belief in it is obligatory, and asking about it is an innovation.' And he said to the questioner: 'I see you are nothing but misguided.' And he ordered that he be slapped (1) and behold, it was Jahm ibn Safwan (may the curse of Allah be upon him).
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
In this brief but authoritative passage, Nasafi transmits the famous statement of Imam Malik (d. 795 CE), one of the four great Sunni imams, regarding the proper approach to the attribute of istiwa. Imam Malik's statement is a classic formulation of the Sunni stance on divine attributes: the meaning (istiwa) is known in general, but the modality (kayfiyya) is beyond human comprehension. Belief in the attribute as affirmed in the Quran is obligatory, and inquiring into its modality is an innovation (bid'a). Imam Malik considered such questioning as a sign of misguidance and dealt harshly with the questioner, who turned out to be Jahm ibn Safwan, the founder of the Jahmiyya sect. This passage underscores the principle of tafwid (consigning the modality to Allah) while affirming the attribute.

Key Terms
الاستواء
الكيف
بدعة
جهم بن صفوان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Imam Malik's statement means we cannot affirm any meaning for istiwa, so we must remain completely silent about it.
Correction: Imam Malik clearly says 'al-istiwā ghayru majhūl' – the istiwa is not unknown. He affirms the meaning. The unknown is the modality, not the attribute itself.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Malik's statement, what is the ruling on asking about how istiwa occurs?
A) It is obligatory
B) It is permissible
C) It is an innovation (bid'a)
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
Imam Malik's statement teaches us to affirm the divine attribute of istiwa as it is revealed, to believe in it without asking how, and to avoid speculative questioning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about divine attributes like istiwa, do you find yourself wishing to know 'how'? How does Imam Malik's statement expose the pride in your heart that wants to comprehend the incomprehensible? What would it look like for you to submit without demanding an explanation?
?
Imagine you are in a gathering where someone insists on discussing the 'mechanics' of Allah's establishment over the Throne. Will you remain silent, or will you recall Imam Malik's warning and gently redirect? What is at stake for your own faith if you tolerate that line of questioning?
?
Imam Malik did not merely correct the questioner—he declared him misguided and ordered him slapped. Are you willing to take a firm stand against theological innovation among your peers, or do you avoid conflict to maintain harmony? How does your fear of people's reactions compare to your fear of falling into innovation?

The Mu'tazila Denial of Seeing Allah and Their Proofs
Imam al-Nasafi presents the Mu'tazila denial of ru'ya and enumerates their scriptural proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila position on ru'ya and the three proofs they cite from the Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila deny the vision of Allah using three scriptural proofs.

In this chapter, Imam al-Nasafi sets the stage by stating the disagreement between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna on the possibility of seeing Allah. He then lists the evidence the Mu'tazila bring to support their denial. Understanding these proofs is essential before we examine the Sunni refutation in the next lesson.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on the Mu'tazila claims and the three proofs they present.
Notice the word 'lan' in the verse of Moses.
2
Identify the three proofs
List the three proofs: the verse of Moses, the verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar', and the hadith of Aisha.
Each proof is introduced with 'وكذلك'.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila reasoning
For each proof, consider how the Mu'tazila interpret it to deny ru'ya. The word 'lan' implies perpetual negation.
4
Reflect on the strength of these proofs
These proofs appear strong if taken literally. Think about how a Sunni scholar might respond.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في إثبات رؤية الله تعالى
قالت المعتزلة : لا تجوز الرؤية على الباري تعالى بالأبصار.
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: تجوز.
وحجتهم قوله تعالى خبرا عن موسى عليه السلام: قَالَ رَبِّ أَرِنِي أَنظُرْ إِلَيْكَ قَالَ لَن تَرَننِي وكلمة (لن) للتأبيد، وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الْأَبْصَرَ﴾.
وكذلك رُوي عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أنها قالت: سألت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «هل رأيت ربك ليلة المعراج؟ فقال: لا».
قوله تعالى: فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ اللَّهِ فهل معنى ذلك أن المصلّي أينما ولى وجهه يكون مقابلاً لمكان الله ؟ تعالى الله عما يقولون ، وكذلك قوله: ﴿ وَهُوَ الَّذِي فِي السَّمَاءِ إِلَهُ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَهُ وما شابهها من آياتٍ وأخبار فإنها تُحمل على ما يليق بالله جل جلاله.
ولا يخفى فساد قول من يقول إن الله تعالى في السماء حقيقة، لأن الله تعالى قديم، والسماء محدثة محدودة، فإن كان الله في السماء بالمعنى الحقيقي فأين كان قبل أن يخلق السماء؟ ففساد هذا ظاهر لكل عاقل.
Chapter on proving the vision of Allah. The Mu'tazila said: Vision (ru'ya) of the Creator is not permissible by (physical) eyes. Ahl al-Sunna wa'l-Jama'a said: It is permissible. Their (the Mu'tazila's) proof is His statement, reporting from Moses alayhi salam: 'He said: My Lord, show me (that) I may look at You. He said: You will never see Me.' And the word 'lan' indicates perpetuity. And likewise His statement: 'Vision cannot perceive Him, and He perceives all vision.' And likewise it is narrated from A'isha radiya Allahu anha that she said: 'I asked the Messenger of Allah sallallahu alayhi wa sallam: Did you see your Lord on the night of Mi'raj? He said: No.' His statement: 'Wherever you turn, there is the Face of Allah.' Does that mean that the praying person, wherever he turns his face, he faces the place of Allah? Exalted is Allah above what they say. And likewise His statement: 'And He is the One Who in the heaven is God and on the earth is God,' and similar verses and reports; they are to be interpreted as befits Allah. And it is not hidden the corruption of the statement of whoever says that Allah is truly in the heaven, because Allah is eternal, and the heaven is originated and limited. If Allah were in the heaven in a real sense, then where was He before He created the heaven? The corruption of this is clear to every rational person.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a chapter on proving the possibility of seeing Allah (ru'yat Allah) in the afterlife. The author states the Mu'tazila denial and the Sunni affirmation. Then he lists the Mu'tazila proofs: the verse of Moses with 'lan tarani' implying eternal denial, the verse 'la tudrikuhu al-absar', and the hadith of Aisha. The author then refutes these proofs by showing that the verses they cite are misinterpreted. He explains that the verse 'wherever you turn, there is the Face of Allah' does not imply spatial location, nor does 'in the heaven is God' mean Allah is physically in the sky. He then refutes a literal interpretation of 'fis sama'' by arguing from Allah's eternity: since the heaven is created, if Allah were in it, where was He before its creation? This reductio shows the absurdity of corporealism.

Key Terms
رؤية
معتزلة
أهل السنة والجماعة
لن
الأبصار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which word in the verse to Moses does the Mu'tazila use to argue for perpetual negation of vision?
A) 'lan'
B) 'la'
C) 'ma'
D) 'in'

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila base their denial of seeing Allah on three scriptural proofs: the verse of Moses, the verse of vision, and the hadith of Aisha.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila used the word 'lan' to claim that even Moses could not see Allah. If you were in Moses' place, would that answer satisfy your longing to see your Creator? How does your own yearning for Allah compare to that of a prophet?
?
The Prophet (saw) denied seeing his Lord on the night of Mi'raj. Does that make you doubt that you will ever see Him? Or does it increase your reliance on the Quranic promise that some faces will 'look at their Lord' (75:22-23)? What would it take for you to be certain that you will see Allah?
?
The Mu'tazila argue from Scripture, yet they arrive at a different conclusion from Ahl al-Sunna. When you read the verses they cite, do you feel the weight of their argument? How do you reconcile such texts with the hope of seeing Allah? Is your hope based on evidence or mere desire?

The Sunni Refutation of the Mu'tazila Proofs and the Argument Against Anthropomorphism
Imam al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazila interpretations and disproves anthropomorphism with an argument from eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni scholars refute the Mu'tazila proofs and why literal interpretations of certain verses are rejected.

Core Idea
The verses cited by the Mu'tazila must be interpreted in a way befitting Allah's transcendence.

After presenting the Mu'tazila evidence, Imam al-Nasafi now turns to the Sunni response. He argues that the verses and hadith they cite do not literally deny vision in the afterlife, but rather address specific contexts. Moreover, he refutes a related misconception: that Allah is physically located in heaven. This lesson shows how the same texts are interpreted consistently with tanzih.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the two verses the author addresses.
2
Understand the method
The author first questions literal interpretations, then provides a rational proof. Identify both parts.
3
Follow the rational argument
Trace the argument: Allah is eternal, heaven is created. If Allah were in heaven, where was He before creation? This leads to absurdity.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Apply the principle
Generalize: all verses and reports must be interpreted in a way befitting Allah's majesty, not literally.

Ahl al-Sunna's Proofs for the Vision of Allah
Sanusi enumerates several Sunni proofs for the vision of Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the multiple proofs (Qur'anic, hadith, and rational) that Sunni scholars use to establish the possibility and occurrence of seeing Allah in the afterlife.

Core Idea
The vision of Allah is proven by the Qur'an, sunna, and rational necessity.

The Sunni school affirms that believers will see Allah in Paradise. While some deny this based on God's transcendence, the Sunnis present a range of proofs from revelation and reason. This lesson examines the key arguments from the story of Moses, explicit Qur'anic verses, and a famous hadith, showing that the vision is both possible and promised.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get an overview of the five proofs presented.
Notice the recurring Arabic phrase 'وكذلك' (likewise) linking each proof.
2
Examine the proof from Musa's request
Focus on the argument that prophets are infallible (ma'sūm) and would not ask for something impossible, so Musa's request implies the vision is possible.
This is a rational proof (ḥujja 'aqliyya) based on the principle of prophetic infallibility.
3
Analyze the three Qur'anic verses
Consider each verse: 'Faces looking at their Lord', 'Hope for meeting with their Lord', and 'Whatever your souls desire'. Understand how each supports the vision.
The third verse involves a logical argument: if paradise souls desire vision, it must be granted.
4
Reflect on the hadith
The hadith compares seeing Allah to seeing the full moon without crowding, emphasizing clarity and ease.
This hadith is widely transmitted and serves as a concrete illustration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحجتنا قوله تعالى خبرًا عن موسى عليه السلام: قَالَ رَبِّ أَرِنِي أَنْظُرْ إِلَيْكَ فَلولا أن موسى عَلِمَ جواز رؤية الباري وإلا لما سأل، لأن الأنبياء معصومون مِنْ أن يسألوا سؤالاً مستحيلاً، وكذلك قوله تعالى: وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَيذِ نَاضِرَةٌ إِلَى رَبِّهَا نَاظِرَةٌ وكذلك قوله تعالى: فَمَن كَانَ يَرْجُو القَاءَ رَبِّهِ وكذلك قوله تعالى: وَلَكُمْ فِيهَا مَا تَشْتَهِي أَنفُسُكُمْ فلو اشتهى أهل الجنة إلى الرؤية ولم يروه، يؤدي إلى الخلْفِ في كلام الله تعالى. وكذلك رُوي عن النبي أنه قال: إنكم سترون ربكم كما ترون القمر ليلة البدر لا تُضامُّون في رؤيته أي: لا تزاحمون في رؤيته.
And our proof is the statement of Allah, Most High, reporting from Mūsā, peace be upon him: He said: My Lord, show me (that I may) look at You. If Mūsā did not know the permissibility of seeing the Creator, he would not have asked, because the prophets are infallible from asking an impossible request. Likewise the statement of Allah, Most High: Faces on that day are radiant, looking at their Lord. Likewise His statement: So whoever hopes for the meeting with his Lord. Likewise His statement: And for you therein is whatever your souls desire. So if the people of Paradise desire the vision and do not see it, that would lead to a contradiction in the speech of Allah. And likewise it is narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: You will surely see your Lord as you see the moon on the night of the full moon; you will not be harmed in seeing Him, meaning: you will not be crowded in seeing Him.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents the Sunni proofs (hujaj) for the possibility of seeing Allah. It begins with the verse of Musa: Musa asked to see Allah, and if it were impossible, he would not have asked because prophets are infallible (ma'sūm). Then it cites three verses about the afterlife: (1) 'Faces on that day are radiant, looking at their Lord'—explicitly states looking at Allah; (2) 'Whoever hopes for the meeting with his Lord'—implies that meeting includes vision; (3) 'For you therein is whatever your souls desire'—if the people of Paradise desire vision, it must be granted, otherwise Allah's promise would be broken. Finally, it quotes the famous hadith comparing seeing Allah to seeing the full moon, with the explanation that they will not be crowded (lā tudāmūn). The passage gathers multiple proofs from reason (Musa's request) and revelation.

Key Terms
حجة
عصمة
الأنبياء
النظر إلى الله
الرؤية
لقاء الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that Allah cannot be seen because He is transcendent and the Qur'an says 'lan tarānī' (You will not see Me) to Moses.
Correction: The Sunnis argue that 'lan tarānī' was a statement to Moses in this world, not a denial of vision in the afterlife. Moreover, Moses' request itself shows that the vision is possible; otherwise a prophet would not ask for it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is Musa's request a valid proof for the vision of Allah?
A) Because Allah did not punish him
B) Because prophets are infallible and do not ask for the impossible
C) Because the request was granted
D) Because it is mentioned in the Torah

Key Takeaway
The vision of Allah is established through multiple proofs: the infallibility of prophets, explicit Qur'anic verses, the principle of divine promise, and a prophetic tradition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about Prophet Musa (AS) asking to see Allah with such urgency, what is the most powerful longing in your life right now? How does it compare to this desire for the Divine vision, and will you ask Allah tonight to give you a similar yearning?
?
The hadith says you will see your Lord as clearly as the moon on a full moon night – without any crowding or obstacle. Does your daily life reflect a certainty in that promise, or do you live as if this world is the only reality? What one habit can you change today to live with the vision in mind?
?
If Allah promises to grant the believers whatever they desire in Paradise, including the vision of Himself, what does that say about your relationship with desires in this life? Are you training your soul to desire the highest thing, or are you settling for lesser pleasures while neglecting the ultimate aim?

The Quran: Allah's Eternal Attribute
Nasafi defines the Quran as Allah's eternal attribute and refutes the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Quran is Allah's uncreated speech and attribute, distinct from created letters and sounds.

Core Idea
The Quran is Allah's eternal speech, not a created thing.

Nasafi begins by affirming the Sunni position that the Quran is Allah's attribute, co-eternal with Him. He explicitly refutes the Mu'tazila who claim it is created. This foundational doctrine shapes how Muslims relate to the Quran as divine speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage from the beginning through 'neither it nor other than it' to get the definition and refutation.
Note the strong negation of createdness and physical attributes.
2
Identify the key claims
Notice that Nasafi says the Quran is Allah's speech and attribute, and that Allah with all attributes is eternal, not created.
3
Examine the refutation of Mu'tazila
The passage is explicitly a refutation of those who say the Quran is created. Understand why this distinction matters.
Mu'tazila held that the Quran is created in time.
4
Appreciate the negation of letters and sounds
Nasafi emphasizes that Allah's speech is without letters, sounds, or syllables. These are properties of created speech.
This prevents anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان أن القرءان كلام الله تعالى وفيه الرد على المعتزلة. القرآن كلام الله تعالى وصفته، والله تعالى بجميع صفاته واحد قديم غير محدث ولا مخلوق، بلا حرف ولا صوت ولا مقاطع ولا مبادئ له، لا هو ولا غيره، فأسمعه جبرائيل عليه السلام بالصوت والحروف، فخلق صوتا فسمعه بذلك الصوت والحروف، فحفظه جبرائيل عليه السلام ووعاه، ونقل إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إنزال الوحي والرسالة لا إنزال الشخص والصورة، وتلاه على النبي عليه السلام، فحفظه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ووعاه، وتلاه على أصحابه فحفظوه، وتلوه على التابعين، والتابعون على الصالحين، هكذا حتى وصل إلينا.
Chapter on explaining that the Quran is the speech of Allah, and in it is the refutation of the Mu'tazila. The Quran is the speech of Allah and His attribute. Allah, with all His attributes, is one, eternal, not originated nor created, without letter, without sound, without syllables, without beginning for it, neither it nor other than it. So Gabriel, peace be upon him, caused him to hear it with sound and letters. So He created a sound, and he heard it through that sound and letters. Then Gabriel, peace be upon him, preserved it and memorized it, and conveyed to the Prophet, peace be upon him, the sending down of revelation and the message, not the sending down of a person or a form. And he recited it to the Prophet, peace be upon him, so the Prophet, peace be upon him, memorized it and preserved it. And he recited it to his companions, so they memorized it. And they recited it to the successors, and the successors to the righteous, thus until it reached us.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage defines the Sunni doctrine of the Quran as the uncreated speech of Allah. Nasafi states that the Quran is Allah's attribute, and like all attributes, it is eternal, not created. He emphasizes that Allah's speech is without letters, sounds, or syllables – these are created mediums. Gabriel heard the speech through a created sound, then conveyed the meaning to the Prophet. The Prophet recited it with letters and sounds to the companions, who transmitted it. This chain preserves the Quran's divine origin while acknowledging that its physical expression is created. The passage also explicitly refutes the Mu'tazila, who held that the Quran is created.

Misconception: Some think the Quran's letters and sounds are eternal.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that the Quran as Allah's speech is without letters, sounds, or syllables; these are created mediums.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi say about the Quran's letters and sounds?

C) The Quran has no letters or sounds.
D) They are part of Allah's attribute.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is Allah's eternal speech, not created, and without physical properties like letters or sounds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly internalize that you are engaging with Allah's eternal attribute—not mere words? How would your heart change if you recited with this awareness every time?
?
If the Quran is without letters and sounds in its true essence, why has Allah chosen to manifest it to us in a form we can hear? What does this say about His mercy and desire to communicate with you?
?
The Mu'tazila believed the Quran was created, perhaps to protect Allah's oneness. But have you ever, in practice, treated the Quran as a created book—like any other text—by neglecting its commands or forgetting its divine origin? What would it mean for your daily life to treat it as eternal?

How the Quran Reached Us: Gabriel's Role
Nasafi describes the transmission of the Quran from Allah through Gabriel to the Prophet and the chain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the process by which Gabriel conveyed the eternal Quran to the Prophet through created sounds and letters, and the subsequent transmission chain.

Core Idea
Gabriel heard Allah's speech through a created sound and conveyed it to the Prophet.

After establishing the Quran's eternal nature, Nasafi explains how it was transmitted to humanity. He describes that Allah created a sound through which Gabriel heard the speech, then Gabriel recited it to the Prophet with letters and sounds. The Prophet then taught it to the companions, who passed it down, ensuring its preservation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on transmission
Read from 'So Gabriel...' to the end to understand the chain.
2
Understand the distinction
Note that the eternal speech was heard through a created sound and letters. This preserves the uncreated nature while allowing transmission.
3
Follow the chain
Trace the line: Allah -> Gabriel -> Prophet -> Companions -> Successors -> Us.
It is an oral transmission, not a physical object.
4
Identify what was sent down
Nasafi stresses it was the sending down of revelation and message, not a person or form.
Refutes the idea of a physical Quran descending.
